Composition Analyser</td></tr><tr><th scope="row">LAP</th><td>Lyman Alpha Photometer</td></tr></tbody></table></td></tr><tr><td colspan="2" style="text-align:center"><div class="" style="width:100%; text-align:center; border-top:1px #aaa solid">Indian missions to Mars</div><div style="width:100%"><div class="noprint" style="float: right; text-align:right;padding-left:0.5em;"><a href="/wiki/Mars_Orbiter_Mission_2" title="Mars Orbiter Mission 2">Mars Orbiter Mission 2</a>&#160;&#8594;</div></div>&#160;</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>The <b>Mars Orbiter Mission</b> (<b>MOM</b>), also called <i><b>Mangalyaan</b></i> ("Mars-craft", from <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sanskrit_language" title="Sanskrit language">Sanskrit</a>: <span lang="sa">&#2350;&#2306;&#2327;&#2354;</span> <i>mangala</i>, "Mars" and &#2351;&#2366;&#2344; <i>y&#257;na</i>, "craft, vehicle"),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Sanskrit_10-0"><a href="#cite_note-Sanskrit-10">[10]</a></sup> is a <a href="/wiki/Space_probe" title="Space probe">space probe</a> orbiting <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> since 24 September 2014. It was launched on 5 November 2013 by the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Space_Research_Organisation" title="Indian Space Research Organisation">Indian Space Research Organisation</a> (ISRO).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pro_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Pro-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-India-20120815_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-India-20120815-12">[12]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20120830_13-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20120830-13">[13]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20131123_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20131123-14">[14]</a></sup> It is <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">India</a>\'s first interplanetary mission<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20140925-ED_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20140925-ED-15">[15]</a></sup> and it made it the fourth <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_space_agencies" title="List of space agencies">space agency</a> to reach Mars, after <a href="/wiki/Roscosmos" title="Roscosmos">Roscosmos</a>, <a href="/wiki/NASA" title="NASA">NASA</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/European_Space_Agency" title="European Space Agency">European Space Agency</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> It is the first Asian nation to reach Mars orbit, and the first nation in the world to do so in its first attempt.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NYT-20140924-GH_21-0"><a href="#cite_note-NYT-20140924-GH-21">[21]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Mars Orbiter Mission probe lifted-off from the <a href="/wiki/Satish_Dhawan_Space_Centre_First_Launch_Pad" title="Satish Dhawan Space Centre First Launch Pad">First Launch Pad</a> at <a href="/wiki/Satish_Dhawan_Space_Centre" title="Satish Dhawan Space Centre">Satish Dhawan Space Centre</a> (<a href="/wiki/Sriharikota" title="Sriharikota">Sriharikota</a> Range SHAR), <a href="/wiki/Andhra_Pradesh" title="Andhra Pradesh">Andhra Pradesh</a>, using a <a href="/wiki/Polar_Satellite_Launch_Vehicle" title="Polar Satellite Launch Vehicle">Polar Satellite Launch Vehicle</a> (PSLV) rocket C25 at 09:08&#160;UTC on 5 November 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Launch_window" title="Launch window">launch window</a> was approximately 20 days long and started on 28 October 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-launch_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-launch-5">[5]</a></sup> The MOM probe spent about a month in <a href="/wiki/Geocentric_orbit" title="Geocentric orbit">Earth orbit</a>, where it made a series of seven <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Orbit_raising" title="Orbit raising">apogee-raising</a> <a href="/wiki/Orbital_maneuver" title="Orbital maneuver">orbital manoeuvres</a> before <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trans-Mars_injection" title="Trans-Mars injection">trans-Mars injection</a> on 30 November 2013 (<a href="/wiki/Coordinated_Universal_Time" title="Coordinated Universal Time">UTC</a>).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-isro20131202_23-0"><a href="#cite_note-isro20131202-23">[23]</a></sup> After a 298-day transit to Mars, it was inserted into Mars orbit on 24 September 2014.\n</p><p>The mission is a "<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Technology_demonstrator" title="Technology demonstrator">technology demonstrator</a>" project to develop the technologies for designing, planning, management, and operations of an interplanetary mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSDC-201209_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-ISSDC-201209-24">[24]</a></sup> It carries five instruments that will help advance knowledge about Mars to achieve its secondary, scientific objective.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc20140924_25-0"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20140924-25">[25]</a></sup> The spacecraft is currently being monitored from the Spacecraft Control Centre at <a href="/wiki/ISRO_Telemetry,_Tracking_and_Command_Network" title="ISRO Telemetry, Tracking and Command Network">ISRO Telemetry, Tracking and Command Network</a> (ISTRAC) in <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bengaluru</a> with support from the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Deep_Space_Network" title="Indian Deep Space Network">Indian Deep Space Network</a> (IDSN) antennae at <a href="/wiki/Byalalu" title="Byalalu">Byalalu</a>, Karnataka.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="toc" id="toc"><input class="toctogglecheckbox" id="toctogglecheckbox" role="button" style="display:none" type="checkbox"/><div class="toctitle" class="toctext">Cost</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-3"><a href="#Mission_objectives"><span class="tocnumber">2</span> <span class="toctext">Mission objectives</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-4"><a href="#Scientific_objectives"><span class="tocnumber">2.1</span> <span class="toctext">Scientific objectives</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-5"><a href="#Spacecraft_design"><span class="tocnumber">3</span> <span class="toctext">Spacecraft design</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-6"><a href="#Payload"><span class="tocnumber">4</span> <span class="toctext">Payload</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-7"><a href="#Telemetry_and_command"><span class="tocnumber">5</span> <span class="toctext">Telemetry and command</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-8"><a href="#Communications"><span class="tocnumber">5.1</span> <span class="toctext">Communications</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-9"><a href="#Mission_profile"><span class="tocnumber">6</span> <span class="toctext">Mission profile</span></a>\n<ul>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-10"><a href="#Launch"><span class="tocnumber">6.1</span> <span class="toctext">Launch</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-11"><a href="#Orbit_raising_manoeuvres"><span class="tocnumber">6.2</span> <span class="toctext">Orbit raising manoeuvres</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-12"><a href="#Trans-Mars_injection"><span class="tocnumber">6.3</span> <span class="toctext">Trans-Mars injection</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-13"><a href="#Trajectory_correction_maneuvers"><span class="tocnumber">6.4</span> <span class="toctext">Trajectory correction maneuvers</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-14"><a href="#Mars_orbit_insertion"><span class="tocnumber">6.5</span> <span class="toctext">Mars orbit insertion</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-15"><a href="#Status"><span class="tocnumber">7</span> <span class="toctext">Status</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-16"><a href="#Recognition"><span class="tocnumber">8</span> <span class="toctext">Recognition</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-17"><a href="#Follow-up_mission"><span class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">Follow-up mission</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-18"><a href="#See_also"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-19"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-20"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>On 23 November 2008, the first public acknowledgement of an unmanned mission to Mars was announced by then-ISRO chairman <a href="/wiki/G._Madhavan_Nair" title="G. Madhavan Nair">G. Madhavan Nair</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> The MOM mission concept began with a feasibility study in 2010 by the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Institute_of_Space_Science_and_Technology" title="Indian Institute of Space Science and Technology">Indian Institute of Space Science and Technology</a> after the launch of lunar satellite <a href="/wiki/Chandrayaan-1" title="Chandrayaan-1">Chandrayaan-1</a> in 2008. Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Manmohan_Singh" title="Manmohan Singh">Manmohan Singh</a> approved the project on 3 August 2012,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> after the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Space_Research_Organisation" title="Indian Space Research Organisation">Indian Space Research Organisation</a> completed <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">&#8377;</span>125 crore</span> (US$17&#160;million) of required studies for the orbiter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chennai_30-0"><a href="#cite_note-Chennai-30">[30]</a></sup> The total project cost may be up to <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">&#8377;</span>454 crore</span> (US$63&#160;million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Pro_11-1"><a href="#cite_note-Pro-11">[11]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Dchr_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Dchr-31">[31]</a></sup> The satellite costs <span class="nowrap"><span style="white-space: nowrap">&#8377;</span>153 crore</span> (US$21&#160;million) and the rest of the budget has been attributed to ground stations and relay upgrades that will be used for other ISRO projects.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The space agency had planned the launch on 28 October 2013 but was postponed to 5 November following the delay in ISRO\'s spacecraft tracking ships to take up pre-determined positions due to poor weather in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">Pacific Ocean</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-launch_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-launch-5">[5]</a></sup> Launch opportunities for a fuel-saving <a href="/wiki/Hohmann_transfer_orbit" title="Hohmann transfer orbit">Hohmann transfer orbit</a> occur every 26 months, in this case the next two would be in 2016 and 2018.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph20120816_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph20120816-33">[33]</a></sup>\n</p><p>Assembly of the PSLV-XL launch vehicle, designated C25, started on 5 August 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOIAssly1_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-TOIAssly1-34">[34]</a></sup> The mounting of the five scientific instruments was completed at <a href="/wiki/Indian_Space_Research_Organisation_Satellite_Centre" title="Indian Space Research Organisation Satellite Centre">Indian Space Research Organisation Satellite Centre</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangalore" title="Bangalore">Bengaluru</a>, and the finished spacecraft was shipped to Sriharikota on 2 October 2013 for integration to the PSLV-XL launch vehicle.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOIAssly1_34-1"><a href="#cite_note-TOIAssly1-34">[34]</a></sup> The satellite\'s development was fast-tracked and completed in a record 15 months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NDTV_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-NDTV-35">[35]</a></sup> Despite the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/United_States_federal_government_shutdown_of_2013" title="United States federal government shutdown of 2013">US federal government shutdown</a>, NASA reaffirmed on 5 October 2013 it would provide communications and navigation support to the mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> During a meeting on 30 September 2014, NASA and ISRO officials signed an agreement to establish a pathway for future joint missions to explore Mars. One of the working group\'s objectives will be to explore potential coordinated observations and science analysis between the <a href="/wiki/MAVEN" title="MAVEN">MAVEN</a> orbiter and MOM, as well as other current and future Mars missions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cost">Cost</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cost">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The total cost of the mission was approximately <span style="white-space: nowrap">&#8377;</span>450 <a href="/wiki/Crore" title="Crore">Crore</a> (<span style="white-space: nowrap">US$73 million</span>),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ibtimes20131105_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-ibtimes20131105-38">[38]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ndtv20131105_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-ndtv20131105-39">[39]</a></sup> making it the least-expensive Mars mission to date.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-csmon20131105_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-csmon20131105-40">[40]</a></sup> The low cost of the mission was ascribed by <a href="/wiki/K._Radhakrishnan" title="K. Radhakrishnan">K. Radhakrishnan</a>, the chairman of ISRO, to various factors, including a "modular approach", few ground tests and long (18&#8211;20 hour) working days for scientists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/BBC" title="BBC">BBC</a>\'s Jonathan Amos mentioned lower worker costs, home-grown technologies, simpler design, and a significantly less complicated payload than NASA\'s <a href="/wiki/MAVEN" title="MAVEN">MAVEN</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bbc20140924_25-1"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20140924-25">[25]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_objectives">Mission objectives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Mission objectives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mars_Orbiter_Mission_-_India_-_ArtistsConcept.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1500" data-file-width="2254" decoding="async" height="146" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Mars_Orbiter_Mission_-_India_-_ArtistsConcept.jpg/220px-Mars_Orbiter_Mission_-_India_-_ArtistsConcept.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Mars_Orbiter_Mission_-_India_-_ArtistsConcept.jpg/330px-Mars_Orbiter_Mission_-_India_-_ArtistsConcept.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cd/Mars_Orbiter_Mission_-_India_-_ArtistsConcept.jpg/440px-Mars_Orbiter_Mission_-_India_-_ArtistsConcept.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mars_Orbiter_Mission_-_India_-_ArtistsConcept.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Artist\'s rendering of the Mars Orbiter Mission spacecraft, with <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> in the background.</div></div></div>\n<p>The primary objective of the mission is to develop the technologies required for designing, planning, management and operations of an <a href="/wiki/Interplanetary_mission" title="Interplanetary mission">interplanetary mission</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ISSDC-201209_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-ISSDC-201209-24">[24]</a></sup> The secondary objective is to explore Mars\' surface features, <a href="/wiki/Geomorphology" title="Geomorphology">morphology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mineralogy" title="Mineralogy">mineralogy</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Mars" title="Atmosphere of Mars">Martian atmosphere</a> using indigenous scientific instruments.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leonard-Oct2013_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-Leonard-Oct2013-42">[42]</a></sup>\n</p><p><br/>\nThe main objectives are to develop the technologies required for designing, planning, management and operations of an interplanetary mission comprising the following major tasks:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ajey_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ajey-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>42</span></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li>Orbit manoeuvres to transfer the spacecraft from Earth-centred orbit to heliocentric trajectory and finally, capture into Martian orbit</li>\n<li>Development of force models and algorithms for orbit and <a href="/wiki/Attitude_control" title="Attitude control">attitude</a> (orientation)  computations and analysis</li>\n<li>Navigation in all phases</li>\n<li>Maintain the spacecraft in all phases of the mission</li>\n<li>Meeting power, communications, thermal and payload operation requirements</li>\n<li>Incorporate autonomous features to handle contingency situations</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Scientific_objectives">Scientific objectives</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Scientific objectives">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The scientific objectives deal with the following major aspects:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ajey_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ajey-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>43</span></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Exploration_of_Mars" title="Exploration of Mars">Exploration of Mars</a> surface features by studying the morphology, topography and mineralogy</li>\n<li>Study the constituents of Martian atmosphere including <a href="/wiki/Methane" title="Methane">methane</a> and CO<sub>2</sub> using remote sensing techniques</li>\n<li>Study the dynamics of the upper atmosphere of Mars, effects of <a href="/wiki/Solar_wind" title="Solar wind">solar wind</a> and radiation and the escape of volatiles to outer space</li></ul>\n<p>The mission would also provide multiple opportunities to observe the Martian moon <a href="/wiki/Phobos_(moon)" title="Phobos (moon)">Phobos</a> and also offer an opportunity to identify and re-estimate the orbits of asteroids seen during the Martian Transfer Trajectory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ajey_43-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ajey-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>43</span></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Spacecraft_design">Spacecraft design</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Spacecraft design">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><b>Mass</b>: The lift-off mass was 1,337.2&#160;kg (2,948&#160;lb), including 852&#160;kg (1,878&#160;lb) of propellant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Arunan2015_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-Arunan2015-3">[3]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Bus</b>: The spacecraft\'s <a href="/wiki/Satellite_bus" title="Satellite bus">bus</a> is a modified <a href="/wiki/Comparison_of_satellite_buses" title="Comparison of satellite buses">I-1 K</a> structure and propulsion hardware configuration, similar to <a href="/wiki/Chandrayaan-1" title="Chandrayaan-1">Chandrayaan-1</a>, India\'s lunar orbiter that operated from 2008 to 2009, with specific improvements and upgrades needed for a Mars mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Leonard-Oct2013_42-1"><a href="#cite_note-Leonard-Oct2013-42">[42]</a></sup> The satellite structure is constructed of an aluminium and composite fibre reinforced plastic (<a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Carbon-fiber-reinforced_polymer" title="Carbon-fiber-reinforced polymer">CFRP</a>) sandwich construction.</li>\n<li><b>Power</b>: Electric power is generated by three <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Solar_array" title="Solar array">solar array</a> panels of 1.8&#160;m &#215;&#160;1.4&#160;m (5&#160;ft 11&#160;in &#215;&#160;4&#160;ft 7&#160;in) each (7.56&#160;m<sup>2</sup> (81.4&#160;sq&#160;ft) total), for a maximum of 840 watts of power generation in Mars orbit. Electricity is stored in a 36 <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ampere-hour" title="Ampere-hour">Ah</a> <a href="/wiki/Lithium-ion_battery" title="Lithium-ion battery">Lithium-ion battery</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-specifications_2-2"><a href="#cite_note-specifications-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Propulsion</b>: A liquid fuel engine with a thrust of 440 <a href="/wiki/Newton_(unit)" title="Newton (unit)">newtons</a> (99&#160;<a href="/wiki/Pound_(force)" title="Pound (force)">lb<sub>f</sub></a>) is used for orbit raising and insertion into Mars orbit. The orbiter also has eight 22-newton (4.9&#160;lb<sub>f</sub>) thrusters for <a href="/wiki/Attitude_control" title="Attitude control">attitude control</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> Its propellant mass at launch was  852&#160;kg (1,878&#160;lb).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-specifications_2-3"><a href="#cite_note-specifications-2">[2]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Attitude and Orbit Control System</b>: Maneuvering system that includes electronics with a <a href="/wiki/MIL-STD-1750A" title="MIL-STD-1750A">MAR31750</a> processor, two star sensors, a solar panel Sun sensor, a coarse analog Sun sensor, four reaction wheels, and the primary propulsion system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-specifications_2-4"><a href="#cite_note-specifications-2">[2]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Savitha2015_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Savitha2015-46">[46]</a></sup></li>\n<li><b>Antennae</b>: Low gain antenna, mid gain antenna, and high gain antenna<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-specifications_2-5"><a href="#cite_note-specifications-2">[2]</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Payload">Payload</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Payload">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="wikitable" style="float:right; font-family:arial; font-size:11px;">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th colspan="3">Scientific instruments\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>LAP</td>\n<td><i>Lyman-Alpha Photometer</i></td>\n<td>1.97&#160;kg (4.3&#160;lb)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>MSM</td>\n<td><i>Methane Sensor for Mars</i> (defective)<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-repurposed_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-repurposed-47">[47]</a></sup></td>\n<td>2.94&#160;kg (6.5&#160;lb)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>MENCA</td>\n<td><i>Mars Exospheric Neutral <br/>Composition Analyser</i></td>\n<td>3.56&#160;kg (7.8&#160;lb)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>TIS</td>\n<td><i>Thermal Infrared Imaging Spectrometer</i></td>\n<td>3.20&#160;kg (7.1&#160;lb)\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>MCC</td>\n<td><i>Mars Colour Camera</i></td>\n<td>1.27&#160;kg (2.8&#160;lb)\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:327px;"><div class="PopUpMediaTransform" id="mwe_player_0" style="width:325px;" videopayload=\'&lt;div class="mediaContainer" style="width:614px"&gt;&lt;video id="mwe_player_1" poster="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Assembly_Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission.webm/614px--Assembly_Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission.webm.jpg" controls="" preload="none" autoplay="" style="width:614px;height:480px" class="kskin" data-durationhint="600.704" data-startoffset="0" data-mwtitle="Assembly_Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission.webm" data-mwprovider="wikimediacommons"&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/e/e0/Assembly_Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission.webm/Assembly_Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission.webm.480p.vp9.webm#t=00:00:03,00:09:37" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="Small WebM (240P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 240P" data-transcodekey="240p.webm" data-width="306" data-height="240" data-bandwidth="153984" data-framerate="29.97"/&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/e/e0/Assembly_Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission.webm/Assembly_Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission.webm.360p.vp9.webm#t=00:00:03,00:09:37" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp9, opus&amp;quot;" data-title="VP9 (360P)" data-shorttitle="VP9 360P" data-transcodekey="360p.vp9.webm" data-width="460" data-height="360" data-bandwidth="130696" data-framerate="29.97"/&gt;&lt;source src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/transcoded/e/e0/Assembly_Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission.webm/Assembly_Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission.webm.360p.webm#t=00:00:03,00:09:37" type="video/webm; codecs=&amp;quot;vp8, vorbis&amp;quot;" data-title="WebM (360P)" data-shorttitle="WebM 360P" data-transcodekey="360p.webm" data-width="460" data-height="360" data-bandwidth="266280" data-framerate="29.97"/&gt;&lt;/video&gt;&lt;/div&gt;\'><img alt="File:Assembly Animation of Mars Orbiter Mission.webm" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e0/Assembly_Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission.webm/325px-seek%3D3-Assembly_Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission.webm.jpg" style="width:325px;height:254px"/><a href="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/e/e0/Assembly_Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission.webm" target="new" title="Play media"><span class="play-btn-large"><span class="mw-tmh-playtext">Play media</span></span></a></div> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Assembly_Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission.webm" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Animated assembly of Mars Orbiter Mission spacecraft</div></div></div>\n<p>The 15&#160;kg (33&#160;lb) scientific payload consists of five instruments:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-payload_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-payload-48">[48]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kumar_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kumar-49">[49]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<ul><li><b>Atmospheric studies:</b>\n<ul><li>Lyman-Alpha Photometer (LAP) &#8211; a <a href="/wiki/Photometer" title="Photometer">photometer</a> that measures the relative abundance of <a href="/wiki/Deuterium" title="Deuterium">deuterium</a> and <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a> from <a href="/wiki/Lyman-alpha_line" title="Lyman-alpha line">Lyman-alpha emissions</a> in the upper atmosphere. Measuring the deuterium/hydrogen ratio will allow an estimation of the amount of water loss to <a href="/wiki/Outer_space" title="Outer space">outer space</a>. The nominal plan to operate LAP is between the ranges of approximately 3,000&#160;km (1,900&#160;mi) before and after Mars periapsis. Minimum observation duration for achieving LAP\'s science goals is 60 minutes per orbit during normal range of operation. The objectives of this instrument are as follows:<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ajey_43-3"><a href="#cite_note-Ajey-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>56,57</span></sup>\n<ul><li>Estimation of D/H ratio</li>\n<li>Estimation of escape flux of H2 corona</li>\n<li>Generation of <a href="/wiki/Hydrogen" title="Hydrogen">hydrogen</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deuterium" title="Deuterium">deuterium</a> coronal profiles.</li></ul></li>\n<li>Methane Sensor for Mars (MSM) &#8211; was meant to measure <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Mars#Methane" title="Atmosphere of Mars">methane in the atmosphere of Mars</a>, if any, and map its sources with an accuracy of parts-per-billion (ppb).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-payload_48-1"><a href="#cite_note-payload-48">[48]</a></sup> After entering Mars orbit it was determined that the instrument, although in good working condition, had a design flaw and it was not capable of detecting methane.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-repurposed_47-1"><a href="#cite_note-repurposed-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ajey_43-4"><a href="#cite_note-Ajey-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>57</span></sup> The instrument was repurposed as an albedo mapper.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-repurposed_47-2"><a href="#cite_note-repurposed-47">[47]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></li></ul></li>\n<li><b>Particle environment studies:</b>\n<ul><li>Mars Exospheric Neutral Composition Analyser (MENCA) &#8211; is a <a href="/wiki/Quadrupole_mass_analyzer" title="Quadrupole mass analyzer">quadrupole mass analyser</a> capable of analysing the neutral composition of particles in the range of 1&#8211;300 amu (atomic mass unit) with unit mass resolution. The heritage of this payload is from Chandra\'s Altitudinal Composition Explorer (CHACE) payload aboard the Moon Impact Probe (MIP) in <a href="/wiki/Chandrayaan-1" title="Chandrayaan-1">Chandrayaan-1</a> mission. MENCA is planned to perform five observations per orbit with one hour per observation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ajey_43-5"><a href="#cite_note-Ajey-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>58</span></sup></li></ul></li>\n<li><b>Surface imaging studies:</b>\n<ul><li>Thermal Infrared Imaging Spectrometer (TIS) &#8211; TIS measures the thermal emission and can be operated during both day and night. It would map surface composition and mineralogy of Mars and also monitor atmospheric CO<span style="display:inline-block; margin-bottom:-0.3em; vertical-align:-0.4em; line-height:1.2em; font-size:70%; text-align:left;"><br/>2</span> and turbidity (required for the correction of MSM data). Temperature and emissivity are the two basic physical parameters estimated from thermal emission measurement. Many minerals and soil types have characteristic spectra in TIR region. TIS can map surface composition and mineralogy of Mars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ajey_43-6"><a href="#cite_note-Ajey-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>59</span></sup></li>\n<li>Mars Colour Camera (MCC) &#8211; This tricolour camera gives images and information about the surface features and composition of Martian surface. It is useful to monitor the dynamic events and weather of Mars like dust storms/atmospheric turbidity. MCC will also be used for probing the two satellites of Mars, <a href="/wiki/Phobos_(moon)" title="Phobos (moon)">Phobos</a> and <a href="/wiki/Deimos_(moon)" title="Deimos (moon)">Deimos</a>. MCC would provide context information for other science payloads. MCC images are to be acquired whenever MSM and TIS data is acquired. Seven Apoareion Imaging of the entire disc and multiple Periareion images of 540&#160;km &#215;&#160;540&#160;km (340&#160;mi &#215;&#160;340&#160;mi) are planned in every orbit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ajey_43-7"><a href="#cite_note-Ajey-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>58</span></sup></li></ul></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Telemetry_and_command">Telemetry and command</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Telemetry and command">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Telemetry" title="Telemetry">Telemetry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Telecommand" title="Telecommand">Telecommand</a></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/ISRO_Telemetry,_Tracking_and_Command_Network" title="ISRO Telemetry, Tracking and Command Network">ISRO Telemetry, Tracking and Command Network</a> performed navigation and tracking operations for the launch with ground stations at <a href="/wiki/Sriharikota" title="Sriharikota">Sriharikota</a>, <a href="/wiki/Port_Blair" title="Port Blair">Port Blair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brunei" title="Brunei">Brunei</a> and <a href="/wiki/Biak" title="Biak">Biak</a> in <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> and after the spacecraft\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apogee" title="Apogee">apogee</a> became more than 100,000&#160;km, an 18&#160;m (59&#160;ft) and a 32&#160;m (105&#160;ft) diameter antenna of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Deep_Space_Network" title="Indian Deep Space Network">Indian Deep Space Network</a> were utilised.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thin6n13_53-0"><a href="#cite_note-thin6n13-53">[53]</a></sup> The 18&#160;m (59&#160;ft) dish antenna was used for communication with the craft until April 2014, after which the larger 32&#160;m (105&#160;ft) antenna was used.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thin1052_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-thin1052-54">[54]</a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Deep_Space_Network" title="Deep Space Network">NASA\'s Deep Space Network</a> is providing position data through its three stations located in <a href="/wiki/Canberra" title="Canberra">Canberra</a>, <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">Madrid</a> and <a href="/wiki/Goldstone_Deep_Space_Communications_Complex" title="Goldstone Deep Space Communications Complex">Goldstone</a> on the US West Coast during the non-visible period of ISRO\'s network.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/South_African_National_Space_Agency" title="South African National Space Agency">South African National Space Agency</a>\'s (SANSA) <a href="/wiki/Hartebeesthoek_Radio_Astronomy_Observatory" title="Hartebeesthoek Radio Astronomy Observatory">Hartebeesthoek</a> (HBK) ground station is also providing satellite tracking, telemetry and command services.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-56"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Communications are handled by two 230-watt <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/TWTA" title="TWTA">TWTAs</a> and two <a href="/wiki/Unified_S-band#Coherent_transponders_and_Doppler_tracking" title="Unified S-band">coherent transponders</a>. The antenna array consists of a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Low-gain_antenna" title="Low-gain antenna">low-gain antenna</a>, a medium-gain antenna and a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/High-gain_antenna" title="High-gain antenna">high-gain antenna</a>. The high-gain antenna system is based on a single 2.2-metre (7&#160;ft 3&#160;in) reflector illuminated by a feed at <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/S-band" title="S-band">S-band</a>. It is used to transmit and receive the telemetry, tracking, commanding and data to and from the <a href="/wiki/Indian_Deep_Space_Network" title="Indian Deep Space Network">Indian Deep Space Network</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-specifications_2-6"><a href="#cite_note-specifications-2">[2]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Mission_profile">Mission profile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Mission class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph20120816_33-1"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph20120816-33">[33]</a></sup> around the Sun to reach Mars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-thin1052_54-1"><a href="#cite_note-thin1052-54">[54]</a></sup> This phase plan included up to four trajectory corrections if needed.\n</td>\n<td><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a id="cite_ref-Isroprel_8-3"><a href="#cite_note-Isroprel-8">[8]</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Launch">Launch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Launch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mars_Orbitor_Mission_Launch.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="450" data-file-width="550" decoding="async" height="180" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Mars_Orbitor_Mission_Launch.jpg/220px-Mars_Orbitor_Mission_Launch.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Mars_Orbitor_Mission_Launch.jpg/330px-Mars_Orbitor_Mission_Launch.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dc/Mars_Orbitor_Mission_Launch.jpg/440px-Mars_Orbitor_Mission_Launch.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mars_Orbitor_Mission_Launch.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Launch of the Mars Orbiter Mission</div></div></div>\n<p>As originally conceived, ISRO was to launch MOM on its <a href="/wiki/Geosynchronous_Satellite_Launch_Vehicle" title="Geosynchronous Satellite Launch Vehicle">Geosynchronous Satellite Launch Vehicle</a> (GSLV),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lakdawalla_Oct_30_76-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lakdawalla_Oct_30-76">[76]</a></sup> but as the GSLV failed twice in 2010 and ISRO was continuing to sort out issues with its <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cryogenic_engine" title="Cryogenic engine">cryogenic engine</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> it was not advisable to wait for the new batch of rockets as that would have delayed the MOM project for at least three years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> ISRO opted to switch to the less-powerful <a href="/wiki/Polar_Satellite_Launch_Vehicle" title="Polar Satellite Launch Vehicle">Polar Satellite Launch Vehicle</a> (PSLV). Since the PSLV was not powerful enough to place MOM on a direct-to-Mars trajectory, the spacecraft was launched into a highly elliptical Earth orbit and used its own thrusters over multiple perigee burns (to take advantage of the <a href="/wiki/Oberth_effect" title="Oberth effect">Oberth effect</a>) to place itself on a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trans-Mars_injection" title="Trans-Mars injection">trans-Mars trajectory</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lakdawalla_Oct_30_76-1"><a href="#cite_note-Lakdawalla_Oct_30-76">[76]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 19 October 2013, ISRO chairman <a href="/wiki/K._Radhakrishnan" title="K. Radhakrishnan">K. Radhakrishnan</a> announced that the launch had to be postponed by a week as a result of a delay of a crucial telemetry ship reaching <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>. The launch was rescheduled for 5 November 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-launch_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-launch-5">[5]</a></sup> ISRO\'s PSLV-XL placed the satellite into Earth orbit at 09:50&#160;UTC on 5 November 2013,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Chennai_30-1"><a href="#cite_note-Chennai-30">[30]</a></sup> with a perigee of 264.1&#160;km (164.1&#160;mi), an apogee of 23,903.6&#160;km (14,853.0&#160;mi), and inclination of 19.20 degrees,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ET0611_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-ET0611-57">[57]</a></sup> with both the antenna and all three sections of the solar panel arrays deployed.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOI0611_79-0"><a href="#cite_note-TOI0611-79">[79]</a></sup> During the first three orbit raising operations, ISRO progressively tested the spacecraft systems.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOI111113-1_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-TOI111113-1-63">[63]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The orbiter\'s dry mass is 500&#160;kg (1,100&#160;lb), and it carried 852&#160;kg (1,878&#160;lb) of fuel and oxidiser at launch. Its main engine, which is a derivative of the system used on India\'s communications satellites, uses the bipropellant combination <a href="/wiki/Monomethylhydrazine" title="Monomethylhydrazine">monomethylhydrazine</a> and <a href="/wiki/Dinitrogen_tetroxide" title="Dinitrogen tetroxide">dinitrogen tetroxide</a> to achieve the thrust necessary for <a href="/wiki/Escape_velocity" title="Escape velocity">escape velocity</a> from Earth. It was also used to slow down the probe for Mars orbit insertion and, subsequently, for orbit corrections.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Orbit_raising_manoeuvres">Orbit raising manoeuvres</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Orbit raising manoeuvres">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Mars_Orbiter_Mission_ISRO_English.svg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1426" data-file-width="1318" decoding="async" height="238" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Mars_Orbiter_Mission_ISRO_English.svg/220px-Mars_Orbiter_Mission_ISRO_English.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Mars_Orbiter_Mission_ISRO_English.svg/330px-Mars_Orbiter_Mission_ISRO_English.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/05/Mars_Orbiter_Mission_ISRO_English.svg/440px-Mars_Orbiter_Mission_ISRO_English.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Mars_Orbiter_Mission_ISRO_English.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Orbit trajectory diagram (not to scale)</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_trajectory.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="420" data-file-width="560" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_trajectory.gif/220px-Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_trajectory.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_trajectory.gif/330px-Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_trajectory.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_trajectory.gif/440px-Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_trajectory.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_trajectory.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Animation of Mars Orbiter Mission<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> trajectory from 5 November 2013 to 28 March 2015<br/><span style="margin:0; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"><span class="legend-text" style="border:none; padding:1px .6em; background-color:magenta; color:black; font-size:95%; line-height:1.25; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Mars Orbiter Mission</span>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <span style="margin:0; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"><span class="legend-text" style="border:none; padding:1px .6em; background-color:Lime; color:black; font-size:95%; line-height:1.25; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a></span>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <span style="margin:0; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"><span class="legend-text" style="border:none; padding:1px .6em; background-color:RoyalBlue; color:black; font-size:95%; line-height:1.25; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Earth" title="Earth">Earth</a></span>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <span style="margin:0; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"><span class="legend-text" style="border:none; padding:1px .6em; background-color:Yellow; color:black; font-size:95%; line-height:1.25; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Sun" title="Sun">Sun</a></span></div></div></div>\n<p>Several orbit raising operations were conducted from the <a href="/wiki/Master_Control_Facility" title="Master Control Facility">Spacecraft Control Centre</a> (SCC) at the <a href="/wiki/ISRO_Telemetry,_Tracking_and_Command_Network" title="ISRO Telemetry, Tracking and Command Network">ISRO Telemetry, Tracking and Command Network</a> (ISTRAC) at Peenya, Bengaluru on 6, 7, 8, 10, 12 and 16 November by using the spacecraft\'s on-board propulsion system and a series of perigee burns. The first three of the five planned orbit raising manoeuvres were completed with nominal results, while the fourth was only partially successful. However, a subsequent supplementary manoeuvre raised the orbit to the intended altitude aimed for in the original fourth manoeuvre. A total of six burns were completed while the spacecraft remained in Earth orbit, with a seventh burn conducted on 30 November to insert MOM into a <a href="/wiki/Heliocentric_orbit" title="Heliocentric orbit">heliocentric</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mars_transfer_orbit" title="Mars transfer orbit">orbit</a> for its transit to Mars.\n</p><p>The first orbit-raising manoeuvre was performed on 6 November 2013 at 19:47&#160;UTC when the spacecraft\'s 440-newton (99&#160;lb<sub>f</sub>) <a href="/wiki/Liquid-propellant_rocket" title="Liquid-propellant rocket">liquid</a> engine was fired for 416 seconds. With this engine firing, the spacecraft\'s <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apogee" title="Apogee">apogee</a> was raised to 28,825&#160;km (17,911&#160;mi), with a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Perigee" title="Perigee">perigee</a> of 252&#160;km (157&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOI_0713_58-1"><a href="#cite_note-TOI_0713-58">[58]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The second orbit raising manoeuvre was performed on 7 November 2013 at 20:48&#160;UTC, with a burn time of 570.6 seconds resulting in an apogee of 40,186&#160;km (24,970&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MOM_Updates_59-5"><a href="#cite_note-MOM_Updates-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-IE0813_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-IE0813-60">[60]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The third orbit raising manoeuvre was performed on 8 November 2013 at 20:40&#160;UTC, with a burn time of 707 seconds, resulting in an apogee of 71,636&#160;km (44,513&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MOM_Updates_59-6"><a href="#cite_note-MOM_Updates-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-HT0911_61-1"><a href="#cite_note-HT0911-61">[61]</a></sup>\n</p><p>The fourth orbit raising manoeuvre, starting at 20:36&#160;UTC on 10 November 2013, imparted an incremental <a href="/wiki/Delta-v" title="Delta-v">velocity</a> of 35&#160;m/s (110&#160;ft/s) to the spacecraft instead of the planned 135&#160;m/s (440&#160;ft/s) as a result of underburn by the motor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOI111113_62-1"><a href="#cite_note-TOI111113-62">[62]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TPS111013_80-0"><a href="#cite_note-TPS111013-80">[80]</a></sup> Because of this, the apogee was boosted to 78,276&#160;km (48,638&#160;mi) instead of the planned 100,000&#160;km (62,000&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOI111113_62-2"><a href="#cite_note-TOI111113-62">[62]</a></sup> When testing the redundancies built-in for the propulsion system, the flow to the liquid engine stopped, with consequent reduction in incremental velocity. During the fourth orbit burn, the primary and redundant coils of the solenoid flow control valve of 440 newton liquid engine and logic for thrust augmentation by the attitude control thrusters were being tested. When both primary and redundant coils were energised together during the planned modes, the flow to the liquid engine stopped. Operating both the coils simultaneously is not possible for future operations, however they could be operated independently of each other, in sequence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOI111113-1_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-TOI111113-1-63">[63]</a></sup>\n</p><p>As a result of the fourth planned burn coming up short, an additional unscheduled burn was performed on 12 November 2013 that increased the apogee to 118,642&#160;km (73,721&#160;mi),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MOM_Updates_59-7"><a href="#cite_note-MOM_Updates-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TOI111113-1_63-3"><a href="#cite_note-TOI111113-1-63">[63]</a></sup> a slightly higher altitude than originally intended in the fourth manoeuvre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MOM_Updates_59-8"><a href="#cite_note-MOM_Updates-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timesofindia.indiatimes.com_81-0"><a href="#cite_note-timesofindia.indiatimes.com-81">[81]</a></sup> The apogee was raised to 192,874&#160;km (119,846&#160;mi) on 15 November 2013, 19:57&#160;UTC in the final orbit raising manoeuvre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MOM_Updates_59-9"><a href="#cite_note-MOM_Updates-59">[59]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-timesofindia.indiatimes.com_81-1"><a href="#cite_note-timesofindia.indiatimes.com-81">[81]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trans-Mars_injection">Trans-Mars injection</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Trans-Mars injection">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Further information: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Trans-Mars_injection" title="Trans-Mars injection">Trans-Mars injection</a></div>\n<p>On 30 November 2013 at 19:19&#160;UTC, a 23-minute engine firing initiated the <a href="/wiki/Hohmann_transfer_orbit" title="Hohmann transfer orbit">transfer</a> of MOM away from Earth orbit and on <a href="/wiki/Heliocentric_orbit" title="Heliocentric orbit">heliocentric</a> trajectory toward Mars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-isro20131202_23-1"><a href="#cite_note-isro20131202-23">[23]</a></sup> The probe travelled a distance of 780,000,000 kilometres (480,000,000&#160;mi) to reach Mars.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Trajectory_correction_maneuvers">Trajectory correction maneuvers</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Trajectory correction maneuvers">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Four trajectory corrections were originally planned, but only three were carried out.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TPS-EL_66-4"><a href="#cite_note-TPS-EL-66">[66]</a></sup> The first trajectory correction manoeuvre (TCM) was carried out on 11 December 2013 at 01:00&#160;UTC by firing the 22-newton (4.9&#160;lb<sub>f</sub>) thrusters for a duration of 40.5 seconds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MOM_Updates_59-10"><a href="#cite_note-MOM_Updates-59">[59]</a></sup> After this event, MOM was following the designed trajectory so closely that the trajectory correction manoeuvre planned in April 2014 was not required. The second trajectory correction manoeuvre was performed on 11 June 2014 at 11:00&#160;UTC by firing the spacecraft\'s 22 newton thrusters for a duration of 16 seconds.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-update_june_83-0"><a href="#cite_note-update_june-83">[83]</a></sup> The third planned trajectory correction manoeuvre was postponed, due to the orbiter\'s trajectory closely matching the planned trajectory.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-update_tcm_august_84-0"><a href="#cite_note-update_tcm_august-84">[84]</a></sup> The third trajectory correction was also a deceleration test 3.9 seconds long on 22 September 2014.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-TestFire_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-TestFire-75">[75]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mars_orbit_insertion">Mars orbit insertion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Mars orbit insertion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_trajectory_around_Mars.gif"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="420" data-file-width="560" decoding="async" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_trajectory_around_Mars.gif/220px-Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_trajectory_around_Mars.gif" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_trajectory_around_Mars.gif/330px-Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_trajectory_around_Mars.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3d/Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_trajectory_around_Mars.gif/440px-Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_trajectory_around_Mars.gif 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Animation_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_trajectory_around_Mars.gif" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Animation of Mars Orbiter Mission<span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">\'s</span> trajectory around <a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a> from 1 August 2014 to 1 December 2018<br/><span style="margin:0; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"><span class="legend-text" style="border:none; padding:1px .6em; background-color:magenta; color:black; font-size:95%; line-height:1.25; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;Mars Orbiter Mission</span>&#160;<b>&#183;</b> <span style="margin:0; font-size:90%; white-space:nowrap;"><span class="legend-text" style="border:none; padding:1px .6em; background-color:Lime; color:black; font-size:95%; line-height:1.25; text-align:center;">&#160;</span>&#160;<a href="/wiki/Mars" title="Mars">Mars</a></span></div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PM_witnesses_the_insertion_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_into_Martian_orbit.jpg"><img alt="" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/df/PM_witnesses_the_insertion_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_into_Martian_orbit.jpg/440px-PM_witnesses_the_insertion_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_into_Martian_orbit.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PM_witnesses_the_insertion_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_into_Martian_orbit.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>PM Narendra Modi witnesses the insertion of the spacecraft into Martian orbit</div></div></div>\n<p>The plan was for an insertion into <a href="/wiki/Areocentric_orbit" title="Areocentric orbit">Mars orbit</a> on 24 September 2014,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-prelaunch_Oct_2013_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-prelaunch_Oct_2013-7">[7]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MOI_85-0"><a href="#cite_note-MOI-85">[85]</a></sup> approximately 2 days after the arrival of NASA\'s <a href="/wiki/MAVEN" title="MAVEN">MAVEN</a> orbiter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-86"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> The 440-newton liquid apogee motor was test fired on 22 September at 09:00&#160;UTC for 3.968 seconds, about 41 hours before actual orbit insertion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MOI_85-1"><a href="#cite_note-MOI-85">[85]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="wikitable">\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Date\n</th>\n<th>Time (UTC)\n</th>\n<th>Event\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="1">23 September 2014\n</td>\n<td>10:47:32\n</td>\n<td>Satellite communication switched to medium gain antenna\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td rowspan="5">24 September 2014\n</td>\n<td>01:26:32\n</td>\n<td>Forward rotation started for deceleration burn\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>01:42:19\n</td>\n<td>Eclipse started\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>01:44:32\n</td>\n<td><a href="/wiki/Attitude_control" title="Attitude control">Attitude control</a> manoeuvre performed with thrusters\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>01:47:32\n</td>\n<td>Liquid Apogee Motor starts firing\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>02:11:46\n</td>\n<td>Liquid Apogee Motor stops firing\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p>After these events, the spacecraft performed a reverse manoeuvre to reorient from its deceleration burn and entered Martian orbit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Isroprel_8-4"><a href="#cite_note-Isroprel-8">[8]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wapo20140924_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-wapo20140924-4">[4]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Status">Status</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Status">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:One_of_the_first_images_of_the_surface_of_Mars_taken_by_the_Mangalyaan_on_September_25,_2014.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="600" data-file-width="600" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/One_of_the_first_images_of_the_surface_of_Mars_taken_by_the_Mangalyaan_on_September_25%2C_2014.jpg/330px-One_of_the_first_images_of_the_surface_of_Mars_taken_by_the_Mangalyaan_on_September_25%2C_2014.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fe/One_of_the_first_images_of_the_surface_of_Mars_taken_by_the_Mangalyaan_on_September_25%2C_2014.jpg/440px-One_of_the_first_images_of_the_surface_of_Mars_taken_by_the_Mangalyaan_on_September_25%2C_2014.jpg on 25 September 2014</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Arsia_Mons_-_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_(30108068296).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="2048" decoding="async" height="220" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/28/Arsia_Mons_-_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_%2830108068296%29.png/220px-Arsia_Mons_-_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_%2830108068296%29.png" Mons</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Syrtis_Major_-_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_(29512601624).png"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2383" //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/6c/Syrtis_Major_-_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_%2829512601624%29.png/440px-Syrtis_Major_-_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_%2829512601624%29.png 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Syrtis_Major_-_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_(29512601624).png" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Three frame Mars Orbiter Mission Mars Color Camera mosaic of the Syrtis Major region on September 24, 2015.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:The_Chairman,_ISRO,_Shri_A.S._Kiran_Kumar_releasing_the_Mars_Atlas_on_the_occasion_of_the_completion_of_one_year_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_in_Orbit,_in_Bangalore._The_Scientific_Secretary,_ISRO,_Dr._Y.V.N._Krishnamoorthy.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="992" data-file-width="2200" decoding="async" height="99" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/The_Chairman%2C_ISRO%2C_Shri_A.S._Kiran_Kumar_releasing_the_Mars_Atlas_on_the_occasion_of_the_completion_of_one_year_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_in_Orbit%2C_in_Bangalore._The_Scientific_Secretary%2C_ISRO%2C_Dr._Y.V.N._Krishnamoorthy.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/The_Chairman%2C_ISRO%2C_Shri_A.S._Kiran_Kumar_releasing_the_Mars_Atlas_on_the_occasion_of_the_completion_of_one_year_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_in_Orbit%2C_in_Bangalore._The_Scientific_Secretary%2C_ISRO%2C_Dr._Y.V.N._Krishnamoorthy.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/ad/The_Chairman%2C_ISRO%2C_Shri_A.S._Kiran_Kumar_releasing_the_Mars_Atlas_on_the_occasion_of_the_completion_of_one_year_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_in_Orbit%2C_in_Bangalore._The_Scientific_Secretary%2C_ISRO%2C_Dr._Y.V.N._Krishnamoorthy.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:The_Chairman,_ISRO,_Shri_A.S._Kiran_Kumar_releasing_the_Mars_Atlas_on_the_occasion_of_the_completion_of_one_year_of_Mars_Orbiter_Mission_in_Orbit,_in_Bangalore._The_Scientific_Secretary,_ISRO,_Dr._Y.V.N._Krishnamoorthy.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Chairman, ISRO, Shri A.S. Kiran Kumar releasing the Mars Atlas on the occasion of the completion of one year of Mars Orbiter Mission in Orbit, in Bengaluru. The Scientific Secretary, ISRO, Dr. Y.V.N. Krishnamoorthy</div></div></div>\n<p>The orbit insertion put MOM in a highly elliptical orbit around Mars, as planned, with a period of 72 hours 51 minutes 51 seconds, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Periapsis" title="Periapsis">periapsis</a> of 421.7&#160;km (262.0&#160;mi) and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apoapsis" title="Apoapsis">apoapsis</a> of 76,993.6&#160;km (47,841.6&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Isroprel_8-5"><a href="#cite_note-Isroprel-8">[8]</a></sup> At the end of the orbit insertion, MOM was left with 40&#160;kg (88&#160;lb) of fuel on board, more than the 20&#160;kg (44&#160;lb) necessary for a six-month mission.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-momlife_90-0"><a href="#cite_note-momlife-90">[90]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 28 September 2014, MOM controllers published the spacecraft\'s first global view of Mars. The image was captured by the Mars Colour Camera (MCC).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 7 October 2014, the ISRO altered MOM\'s orbit so as to move it behind Mars for <a href="/wiki/C/2013_A1" title="C/2013 A1">Comet Siding Spring\'s</a> flyby of the planet on 19 October 2014. The spacecraft consumed 1.9&#160;kg (4&#160;lb) of fuel for the manoeuvre. As a result, MOM\'s apoapsis was reduced to 72,000&#160;km (45,000&#160;mi).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-planetary_92-0"><a href="#cite_note-planetary-92">[92]</a></sup> After the comet passed by Mars, ISRO reported that MOM remained healthy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hindu20141021_93-0"><a href="#cite_note-hindu20141021-93">[93]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 4 March 2015, the ISRO reported that the MSM instrument was functioning normally and are studying Mars\' <a href="/wiki/Albedo" title="Albedo">albedo</a>, the reflectivity of the planet\'s surface. The Mars Colour Camera was also returning new images of the Martian surface.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94">[94]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 24 March 2015, MOM completed its initial six-month mission in orbit around Mars. ISRO extended the mission by an additional six months; the spacecraft has 37&#160;kg (82&#160;lb) of propellant remaining and all five of its scientific instruments are working properly.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-extension_1_96-0"><a href="#cite_note-extension_1-96">[96]</a></sup> The orbiter can reportedly continue orbiting Mars for several years with its remaining propellant.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-indexpress20150415_97-0"><a href="#cite_note-indexpress20150415-97">[97]</a></sup>\n</p><p>A 17-day communications blackout occurred from 6 to 22 June 2015 while Mars\' orbit took it behind the Sun from Earth\'s view.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ajey_43-8"><a href="#cite_note-Ajey-43">[43]</a></sup><sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">:<span>52</span></sup>\n</p><p>On 24 September 2015, ISRO released its "Mars Atlas", a 120-page scientific <a href="/wiki/Atlas" title="Atlas">atlas</a> containing images and data from the Mars Orbiter Mission\'s first year in orbit.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98">[98]</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2016, the first science results of the mission were published in <i><a href="/wiki/Geophysical_Research_Letters" title="Geophysical Research Letters">Geophysical Research Letters</a></i>, presenting measurements obtained by the spacecraft\'s MENCA instrument of the <a href="/wiki/Atmosphere_of_Mars" title="Atmosphere of Mars">Martian exosphere</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-planetary20160302_99-0"><a href="#cite_note-planetary20160302-99">[99]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bhardwaj2016_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bhardwaj2016-100">[100]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 17 January 2017, MOM\'s orbit was altered to avoid the impending eclipse season. With a burn of eight 22&#160;N thrusters for 431 seconds, resulting in a velocity difference of 97.5 metres per second (351&#160;km/h) using 20 kilograms (44&#160;lb) of propellant (leaving 13&#160;kg remaining), eclipses were be avoided until September 2017. The battery is able to handle eclipses of up to 100 minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2017-01-24_SD_101-0"><a href="#cite_note-2017-01-24_SD-101">[101]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 19 May 2017, MOM reached 1,000 days (973 <a href="/wiki/Timekeeping_on_Mars#Sols" title="Timekeeping on Mars">sols</a>) in orbit around Mars. In that time, the spacecraft completed 388 orbits of the planet and relayed more than 715 images back to Earth. ISRO officials stated that it remains in good health.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hindustan20170619_102-0"><a href="#cite_note-hindustan20170619-102">[102]</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 24 September 2018, MOM completed 4 years in its orbit around Mars, although the designed mission life was only six months. Over these years, MOM\'s Mars Colour Camera has captured over 980 images that were released to the public. The probe is still in good health and continues to work nominally.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103">[103]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Recognition">Recognition</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Recognition">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>In 2014, China referred to India\'s successful Mars Orbiter Mission as the "Pride of Asia".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104">[104]</a></sup> The Mars Orbiter Mission team won US-based <a href="/wiki/National_Space_Society" title="National Space Society">National Space Society</a>\'s 2015 <a href="/wiki/Space_Pioneer_Awards" title="Space Pioneer Awards">Space Pioneer Award</a> in the science and engineering category. NSS said the award was given as the Indian agency successfully executed a Mars mission in its first attempt; and the spacecraft is in an elliptical orbit with a high apoapsis where, with its high resolution camera, it is taking full-disk colour imagery of Mars. Very few full disk images have ever been taken in the past, mostly on approach to the planet, as most imaging is done looking straight down in mapping mode. These images will aid planetary scientists.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105">[105]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-106"><a href="#cite_note-106">[106]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107">[107]</a></sup>\n</p><p>An illustration of the Mars Orbiter Mission spacecraft is featured on the reverse of the <a href="/wiki/Indian_2000-rupee_note" title="Indian 2000-rupee note"><span style="white-space: nowrap">&#8377;2,000</span> currency note</a> of India.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Firstpost_2016_108-0"><a href="#cite_note-Firstpost_2016-108">[108]</a></sup>\n</p><p>An image taken by the Mars Orbiter Mission spacecraft was the cover photo of the November 2016 issue of <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/National_Geographic_(magazine)" title="National Geographic (magazine)">National Geographic</a></i> magazine, for their story "Mars: Race to the Red Planet".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Follow-up_mission">Follow-up mission</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Follow-up mission">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>ISRO plans to develop and launch a follow-up mission called <a href="/wiki/Mars_Orbiter_Mission_2" title="Mars Orbiter Mission 2">Mars Orbiter Mission 2</a> (MOM-2 or <i>Mangalyaan-2</i>) with a greater scientific payload to Mars in 2022-2023.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tecake20160128_112-0"><a href="#cite_note-tecake20160128-112">[112]</a></sup> The orbiter will use <a href="/wiki/Aerobraking" title="Aerobraking">aerobraking</a> to reduce <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Apoapsis" title="Apoapsis">apoapsis</a> of its initial orbit and reach an altitude more suitable for scientific observation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Mars_Orbiter_Mission&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright" role="navigation" style="margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em;border:solid #aaa 1px">\n<ul
